[0m[0m[1m[32m    Finished[0m dev [unoptimized + debuginfo] target(s) in 0.01s
[0m[0m[1m[32m     Running[0m `/home/earl/rust/ues/target/debug/ues 1`

Startup Commands: <invoke> may be the command "ues" or "cargo run"

    <invoke>                 - Run interactively, press enter for each step.
    <invoke> <number times>  - Run a number of times, stop at last run, or when no needs can be done and one, or more, cannot.
    <invoke> [h | help]      - Show this list.


Session Commands:

    h | help                 - Help list display (this list).

    cd <dom num>             - Change the curently displayed Domain (CDD) to the given domain number.

    Press Enter (no command) - Satisfy one need that can be done, if any.

    q | exit | quit          - Quit the program.


    aj <act num> <region>    - For an Action in the CDD, and a limited group, print adJacent squares to the groups anchor

    cs <state>               - Change State, an arbitrary change, for the CDD.

    dn <need number>         - Do a particular Need from the can-do need list.

    dcs                      - Display Current State, and domain.  After a number of commands,
                               the current state scrolls off screen, this might be useful.

    fld <path>               - File Load Data.
    fsd <path>               - File Store Data.

    gps <act num> <region>   - Group Print Squares that define the group region, of a given action, of the CDD.

    oa <region>              - Optimal regions Add the given region, of the CDD.
                             - This will fail if the region is a subset of one of the displayed regions.

    od <region>              - Optimal regions Delete the given region, of the CDD.
                             - This will fail if the region is not found or is a displayed intersection.

    ppd <need number>        - Print the Plan Details for a given need number in the can-do list.

    ps <act num>             - Print all Squares for an action, of the CDD.
    ps <act num> <region>    - Print Squares in a given action and region, of the CDD.

    rps <act num> <region>    - Region, Print Squares that are in the given action and region of the CDD.

    run                      - Run until there are no needs that can be done.

    so                       - Start Over.

    ss <act num>                        - Sample the current State, for a given action, for the CDD.
    ss <act num> <state>                - Sample State for a given action and state, for the CDD.
    ss <act num> <state> <result-state> - Sample State, for a given action, state and arbitrary result, for the CDD.

    ta <act-num>             - Take Action with the current state.

    to <region>              - Change the current state TO within a region, by calculating and executing a plan.

    vert                     - Print vertices and edges in domain 0, action 0.

    A domain number is an integer, zero or greater, where such a domain exists. CDD means the Currently Displayed Domain.

    An action number is an integer, zero or greater, where such an action exists.

    A need number is an integer, zero or greater, where such a need exists.

    A state starts with an 's' character, followed by zero, or more, zero and one characters.

    A state can be specified in hexadecimal, like s0xa5.

    A region starts with an 'r' character, followed by zero, or more, zero, one, X or x characters.

    A region, or state, may contain the separator '_', which will be ignored. Leading zeros can be omitted.

    A state can be used instead of a region, it will be translated to a region with no X-bits.

    pn stands for pattern number, the number of different samples. 1 = 1 kind of result, 2 = 2 kinds of results, in order. U = upredictable.

    pnc stands for pattern number confirmed, by enough extra samples.

    If there is an optimal region for the CDD, when no more needs can be done, the program will seek to change the current state
    to be in an optimal region.

    If there is another optimal region the current state is not in, after a (3 * number-regions-in) steps, the program will get bored
    and seek to move the current state to a different optimal region, or to an intersection of optimal regions.

    "P[]" means Plan: No extra actions need to be run, using the current state, run the need action to satisfy the need.
    "P[1,2]" means Plan: Run action 1, then action 2, to change the current state, then run the need action to satisfy the need.
    You start to see these after step 50-60, using previously generated rules, to limit or extend rules, or test contradictory intersections.

    Needs that cannot be done.  Lets say the current state is s00000000, there is a need for s10000000, and an action that changes
    the left-most two bits.  From state s00.. the only option is state s11.. using that action.  Using the command "cs s10<any 6 more bits>"
    will get things moving again.

    After no more needs can be done, optimal region seeking logic will be used.  If there are more than one optimal
    regions, repeatedly pressing enter will increase the boredom duration, and after 3 times the number of optimal regions
    the current state is in, a different optimal region will be sought.
